
   Message Format
  ----------------

  Message #1 of 8199 <"- ASCII Signiture Rebuilt"|"- ASCII Signiture As-Is">*

  <Subject>

  <Date/Time>

  <Person & email address>

  <2 blank separator lines then...>

  <Message - "As-Is">

  <2 blank lines then @'s as divider line>


  * ASCII signitures have been rebuilt where possible.
    Unfortunately Yahoo store messages in a way which means more than 1 space
    is stored as just 1 space. Viewing the message source, and then trying to
    view HTML source in Firefox didn't make any difference.
    Where I have been unable to rebuild the ASCII signitures I have simply put
    "ASCII Signiture As-Is" by the message number.

    Thanks to Andrew Allen for preserving Peter Cahill's ASCII signiture for
    me (see message 1613) in November 1998.

    Thanks to Michael Cox, as I was able to cross-reference some emails from
    the Onelist archives with ones posted to the Yahoo one to reinstate email
    addresses that Yahoo has discarded, and rebuild some ASCII signitures.

	Message #792 of 8176

TOME & Me!

Tue Sep 1, 1998 6:02 am
<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


Hi there,

I just joined the AMOS list! Just how many people read these things? I
hope someone does!

Anyway, I've programmed with AMOS off and on since it first came out 'til
the present day. It used to be just part of my Amiga activities, now it's
about the only thing I use my Amiga for! Better than nothing, though...

I've written some various garbage programs (some useful, most just trivial
experiments) - nothing really worth noting (anybody need a Hexagon drawing
routine? or another AD&D character generator? - didn't think so :)

My first (and really ONLY) attempt at writing a game was some years ago,
making use of the TOME extension. Several versions of AMOS and AMOS PRO
later, and I find that I can't use TOME any more! My version of TOME is
well out of date (I can't remember what it is off hand, but I DO remember
that it's ancient!)

Does anyone know how I can get hold of the latest version of TOME (AMOS PRO
version!)? If not, what would be a good if not better substitute?

Thanks,

Phil 8-)

	Message #796 of 8176

more snow

Tue Sep 1, 1998 9:17 pm
Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>


Rem Orginal from: "Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com> (thanx)

Rem Hello. I'm trying to get this snowfall to work...

Rem AMOS says Array not dimensioned >>> Plot SNOWXPOS(REP),SNOWYPOS(REP),0
Rem Might be more errors...

Rem Maybe some of you brainy guys could help me more with this one too...


NUMFLKS=99
Dim SNOWXPOS(NUMFLKS),SNOWYPOS(NUMFLKS)
Dim SNOWYSPD(NUMFLKS)

Rem Define procedures...

Procedure CLEAR_SNOW
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS
Rem where 0=Background
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP),SNOWYPOS(REP),0
Next REP
End Proc


Rem Initialize the snow...

For REP=0 To NUMFLKS
SNOWXPOS(REP)=Rnd(352)
SNOWYSPD(REP)=-(REP*3) : Rem Note the - sign
Next REP
Rem Create two screens... REAL is buffered, COL is not...
REALSCRN=0 : _COLSCRN=1
Screen Open REALSCRN,320,240,64,Lowres
Double Buffer : Autoback 0 : Bob Update Off
Screen Open _COLSCRN,320,240,64,Lowres
Autoback 0 : Bob Update Off : Screen Hide _COLSCRN
Rem Initialize the screen palettes and load the IFF picture into
Rem REALSCRN. Draw all static images into REALSCRN then...
Screen Copy Logic(REALSCRN) To Physic(_COLSCRN)

Rem Finally we are ready for the action

ALL_DONE=False
Timer=0
Repeat
CLEAR_SNOW
_UPDATESNOW

If Fire(0) Then ALL_DONE=True
If Timer>1200 Then ALL_DONE=True
Screen Swap REALSCRN : Wait Vbl
Until ALL_DONE
Fade 5 : Wait 75
End

Procedure _UPDATESNOW
Shared REALSCRN,_COLSCRN
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS
XSPD=Rnd(4)-2 : YSPD=Rnd(4)+1
TESTXPOS=SNOWXPOS(REP)+XSPD
TESTYPOS=SNOWYPOS(REP)+YSPD
Rem We have the new position, now check for collision...
Screen ColSCRN
TEST=Point(TESTXPOS,TESTYPOS)
Screen REALSCRN
If(TEST<>0) : Rem where 0=Background color
Rem Ahh, the snow has landed!!
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP),SNOWYPOS(REP),SNOWCOLOR
Rem So, we reset this snowflake...
SNOWXPOS(REP)=Rnd(352)
SNOWYPOS(REP)=0
Else
SNOWXPOS(REP)=TESTXPOS
SNOWYPOS(REP)=TESTYPOS
Rem SNOWCOLOR is the color register you're using for the
Rem snow. In my demo, I used YSPD and had a range of
Rem colors from white to a bluish grey. This makes a very
Rem nice effect when the snow builds up.
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP),SNOWYPOS(REP),SNOWCOLOR
End If
Next REP
End Proc


-
greets grok@flashback.net sweden

	Message #798 of 8176

Re: more snow

Tue Sep 1, 1998 5:22 pm
"Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>


On 01-Sep-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
> Rem Hello. I'm trying to get this snowfall to work...

> Rem AMOS says Array not dimensioned >>> Plot SNOWXPOS(REP),SNOWYPOS(REP),0
> Rem Might be more errors...

> NUMFLKS=99
> Dim SNOWXPOS(NUMFLKS),SNOWYPOS(NUMFLKS)
> Dim SNOWYSPD(NUMFLKS)

You need to globalize all your variables when using procedures!

--- Global NUMFLKS, SNOWXPOS(), SNOWYPOS(), SNOWYSPD()

Also the variable SNOWCOLOR is missing!

--- SNOWCOLOR=1
--- Global SNOWCOLOR

> REALSCRN=0 : _COLSCRN=1
> Screen Open REALSCRN,320,240,64,Lowres

You need to load an IFF pic here with some text for the snow to fall on -
backgorund must be color 0. Try with just

--- Cls 0

> Rem We have the new position, now check for collision...
> Screen ColSCRN

Have to be:

--- Screen _COLSCRN

The program still doesn't work that great due to some double buffer stuff.
Rewriting it would mean more work than doing a new routine, so... Try to
disable Double Buffer.

--
rune j. keller - sporuplundsvej 105 - dk-8472 sporup - keller@vip.cybercity.dk

	Message #801 of 8180 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: TOME & Me!

Tue Sep 1, 1998 10:58 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

> My first (and really ONLY) attempt at writing a game was some years
ago,
> making use of the TOME extension. Several versions of AMOS and AMOS
PRO
> later, and I find that I can't use TOME any more! My version of TOME
is
> well out of date (I can't remember what it is off hand, but I DO
remember
> that it's ancient!)

> Does anyone know how I can get hold of the latest version of TOME
(AMOS PRO
> version!)? If not, what would be a good if not better substitute?

Tome eh? I've never used it myself but I've heard that it's slow and
hard to use, is it? Anyway I'm afraid that I've never heard of an AMOS
Pro version, but you could try using the AmosTurbo extention. It doesn't
have any map commands, but it has /fast/ Icon commands (and other fast
drawing commands) Any I've used these icon commands to write a full
screen scrolling routine that can update at full speed, 50 fps, if you
use sprites and 25fps if you use bobs.

If anyone wants to see it then I can post a copy onto the list. (it's
quite big though, and *very* complex)

See ya.

Re: snow that looks like the blitzblank snow !

Wed Sep 2, 1998 12:20 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

> From: Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>

making huge spikes going up the screen and its not very fast, but when
using AmosTurbo commands + compiled I get about 20fps with 200 flakes on

F Point to Point if you don't have AmosTurbo.

	Message #804 of 8180

I have SNOW Idea What I'm on about!

Tue Sep 1, 1998 11:33 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


I hate People who release Progs and say "This Has not Been tested...."

So here goes... "This Has Not Been Tested!"

So email me if it goes wrong... Update Coming soon...

Hide On

Screen Open 0,320,256,64,Lowres

Flash Off

Curs Off

Cls 0

C=2

NU=50

Dim X#(NU),Y#(NU),M#(NU),D#(NU),KEY#(NU),H(320)

For I=0 To NU

X#(I)=Rnd(320)

D#(I)=Rnd(4)-2

Next I

YM=200

Ink 5

Bar 0,YM+1 To 320,256

Do

For I=0 To NU


' Randomablity Variable Being Used...

' Lower the 980 for More Snow at a time....!


If KEY#(I)>980


' The Unplot.... Get Rid of the snow 2 B Updated...


F Plot X#(I),Y#(I),0


' Check if X axis Movement has gone 2 an Extreeme + or -....


If M#(I)=D#(I)


' If so Reset the Target Variable.....


D#(I)=(Rnd(2)+1)*(-Sgn(D#(I)))

Else


' If not Try and Reach the Target Variable (D#) 4 next Time!


If M#(I)<D#(I)

M#(I)=M#(I)+Rnd(1)+0.5

Else

M#(I)=M#(I)-Rnd(1)-0.5

End If


End If


' Randomized amounts of falling speed....


YV=Rnd(6)+1


' Add the X axis Movement Variable 2 the X axis Variable...


X#(I)=X#(I)+M#(I)


' Check 4 X Over Screen Limits....


If X#(I)>320

X#(I)=X#(I)-320

End If

If X#(I)<0

X#(I)=320+X#(I)

End If


' Check And C if Snow Has Landed...


If Y#(I)+YV>YM-H(X#(I))


' See How High the snow is below the new Flake...


If H(X#(I))>Rnd(4)+2

XV=Rnd(2)-1

X#(I)=X#(I)+XV

End If


' The Dead SnowFlake...


F Plot X#(I),YM-H(X#(I)),C


' Reset SnowFlake


H(X#(I))=H(X#(I))+1

KEY#(I)=0

X#(I)=Rnd(320)

Y#(I)=0


Else

' Plot if SnowFlake in Air...


Y#(I)=Y#(I)+YV

F Plot X#(I),Y#(I),C


End If

Else


' Randomability Variable That a SnowFlake will Fall...


KEY#(I)=Rnd(1000)


End If

Next I

Loop



And Not a Procedure in sight 2 slow Ne thing down!

The Snow Piling up doesn't work properley... I mean have U ever Ceen Spikey
Snow? exactly... The version I'm on now Piles the snow so that if there is 2
much...

They Form nice little piles....

I'm also working on a Isometric Version... And Maybe Even a 3d one!

Along with my 3d ShadeClusters Demo!



Bye till next Time... And remeber... A cucumber sandwich may not Save the world
on its own... But with Salad cream any thing is possible!

	Message #805 of 8180

Hey! Ne1 Like Joysticks?

Tue Sep 1, 1998 11:23 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Hey! Look! At this… Ne1 want a piece of code that turns the joystick input 2 +
or -..

Eg.

J=Joy(1) ;J=2 ; Joystick is Down!

K=J-2 ;k=0

P#=J/4.0 ;P#=0.5

P=P# ;P=0

I=Sgn(J) ;I=1

if P#=P ;This isn’t true 0.5<>0

X=Sgn(J-6)*I

End If

If P=0 ;This is true

Y=I*(K+K+1) ;Y=1

End If

Say you push the joystick up it returns y=-1 X=0!

If You Push Joystick Left then X=-1 Y=0

If You Push Joystick left Diagonally Up X=-1 and Y=-1

You Could use this in a game!! Something similar 2 tron!

Where U only need the direction in +1’s or –1’s!

Hello Again! Snow It's not!

Tue Sep 1, 1998 11:38 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Hey! Usefull tip For People Who want 2 scroll... DMA Scrolling doesn't change
speed dependant on what size of graphic it is moving... It may be slow at moving
small stuff... But if say you want 2 scroll a screen on 2 a screen... Screen
copy starts off fast but slows down as U get more of the screen scrolling..
where as doing it by Direct Memory Access doesn't....

So There U Go... If You want 2 Know what I'm on about check out the Logbase(#)
command!
You can Use DMA 4 Tint effects 2!

	Message #808 of 8180

This Is annoying.. I keep recieving my own Mail!!

Tue Sep 1, 1998 11:51 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Hey! Here is more of my Code... This Contains GRAVITY... WIND and ALSORT OF
OTHER STUFF NEEDED 4 GAMES! Read on! BYE!
Hide On
Cls 0
Screen Open 0,320,256,64,Lowres
Colour 1,$0
Flash Off
Curs Off
Degree
Cls 0
Colour 8,$777
Colour 5,$F0
Ink 5
Box 0,0 To 319,201

'    X
'   /W\
'  /---\
' / M|G \
'/-------\

' X,Y Coordinates
X#=100
Y#=100
' Weight Value
WI#=0

' Acceleration Value
AC#=0
' Don't Remove: When ACL#=0 , ACL# Should Really = 1
' Because to get no change from Multiplication
' You should multiply by 1 not 0
' This is the same with weight...
WI#=WI#+1
AC#=AC#+1
' Maximum Force of Gravity
GM#=3.0
' Maximum Speed on Y axis
YM#=7.0-(WI#/2)
' Maximum Speed on X axis
XM#=7.0
' Gravity Increase
GI#=0.1
' Y Thrust Increase
YI#=0.1
' X Thrust Increase
XI#=0.1
' Air Resistance
AR#=0.05
' Wind Value and Direction + or -
WD#=0.0
' Maximum Rate of Wind Change : in seconds
RW=5
' Speed of Wind Change
SW#=0.1
' Maximum Speed of Wind
MS=2
' Fuel Amount
FA#=100
' Wall Repulsion Factor
BW#=0.5

OX=X#
OY=Y#
Do
Ink 0
Plot X#,Y#
Plot OX,OY

If T=0
T=Rnd(RW*60)
WN#=Rnd((2*MS))-MS
Else
Dec T
End If

If WD#<>WN#
If Abs(WN#-WD#)>0.09
WD#=WD#+(Sgn(WN#-WD#)*SW#)
Else
WD#=WN#
End If
WD=(WD#*10)
Ink 0
Bar 280-20,220 To 280+20,230
Ink 2
If WD>0
Bar 280-WD,220 To 280,230
End If
If WD<0
Bar 280,220 To 280-WD,230
End If
End If

OX=X#
OY=Y#

If Key State(78)=-1
If SX#<XM#
SX#=SX#+(XI#*AC#)
End If
Else
If SX#>0
SX#=SX#-AR#
End If
End If
If Key State(79)=-1
If SX#>-XM#
SX#=SX#-(XI#*AC#)
End If
Else
If SX#<0
SX#=SX#+AR#
End If
End If

If Key State(76)=-1 and KEY<>4
If SY#<YM#
SY#=SY#+(YI#/WI#)*(AC#/2)
End If
If SY#>YM#
SY#=YM#
End If
FA#=FA#-Abs(SY#/100)
Else
If SY#>0
SY#=SY#-GI#
End If
End If

If Key State(77)=-1 and KEY<>4
If SY#>-YM#
SY#=SY#-(YI#/WI#)*(AC#/2)
End If
If SY#<-YM#
SY#=-YM#
End If
FA#=FA#-Abs(SY#/100)
Else
If SY#<0
SY#=SY#+GI#
End If
End If

If FA#<0
KEY=4
End If

If GR#<GM#+(WI#)
GR#=GR#+(GI#*WI#)
If GR#>GM#+(WI#)
GR#=GM#+(WI#)
End If
End If

Y#=Y#-SY#+GR#
X#=X#+SX#-WD#

If X#<1 or X#>318
SX#=-(SX#*BW#)
If X#<1
X#=2
Else
X#=317
End If
End If

If Y#>200
Y#=200
SY#=GM#+(WI#)
End If
If Y#<1
Y#=1
SY#=GM#+(WI#)
End If

Ink 8
Plot OX,OY
Ink 2
Plot X#,Y#
FA=FA#
Text 3,9,Str$(FA)-" "

Wait Vbl
Loop

It should work... Damn Can't think of any thing funny 2 say....
Jut herup tiddle whoops....
there U go thats all from Me!
BYE!!!!!!

	Message #813 of 8180 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Hey! Ne1 Like Joysticks?

Wed Sep 2, 1998 2:14 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

> Hey! Look! At this Ne1 want a piece of code that turns the joystick
input 2 + or -..

Hmm, this seemed a bit too complicated, so I decided to check it out
(and I managed to kill 5mins at the same time ;)

I built a timing loop to test the 2 versions :

'different way
Timer=0
For A=0 To 100000
J=Joy(1)
K=J-2
P#=J/4.0
P=P#
I=Sgn(J)
If P#=P
X=Sgn(J-6)*I
End If
If P=0
Y=I*(K+K+1)
End If
Next
Print Timer


' Old way
Timer=0
For A=0 To 100000
X=0 : Y=0
If Jup(1)
Y=-1
End If
If Jdown(1)
Y=1
End If
If Jleft(1)
X=-1
End If
If Jright(1)
X=1
End If
Next
Print Timer

before compiling the Old way was a lot faster, but after compiling it
was a lot closer:

no joystick movement

Old:155
New:143

Holding down on joystick
Old:154
New:193

Although new is quicker when there's no joy activ. it slows down when
the joystick is pressed.

But, 50vbl out of 100000 loops isn't going to make a lot of difference
anyway so you may as well just use whichever you prefer.

	Message #817 of 8180

I SNOW its me again!

Wed Sep 2, 1998 10:26 am
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Hey! My version don't contain wind... and it don't Use Degree either... It seems
2 be faster!

Hide On
Screen Open 0,320,256,8,Lowres
Flash Off
Curs Off
Cls 0

C=2
NU=100
Dim X#(NU),Y#(NU),M#(NU),D#(NU),KEY#(NU),H(320),Z(NU)

For I=0 To NU
X#(I)=Rnd(320)
D#(I)=Rnd(4)-2
Z(I)=Rnd(6)
Next I
Colour 1,$444
Colour 2,$777
Colour 3,$999
Colour 4,$BBB
Colour 5,$DDD
Colour 6,$FFF
Colour 7,$FFF

' level of ground...
YM=200
' Speed of Descent... Maximum movement down
YA=8

Do
For I=0 To NU

' Randomablity Variable Being Used...
' Lower the 980 for More Snow at a time....!

If KEY#(I)>980

' The Unplot.... Get Rid of the snow 2 B Updated...

F Plot X#(I),Y#(I),0

' Check if X axis Movement has gone 2 an Extreeme + or -....

If M#(I)=D#(I)

' If so Reset the Target Variable.....

D#(I)=(Rnd(2)+1)*(-Sgn(D#(I)))
Else

' If not Try and Reach the Target Variable (D#) 4 next Time!

If M#(I)<D#(I)
M#(I)=M#(I)+Rnd(1)+0.5
Else
M#(I)=M#(I)-Rnd(1)-0.5
End If

End If

' Randomized amounts of falling speed....

YV=Rnd(YA)+1

' Add the X axis Movement Variable 2 the X axis Variable...

X#(I)=X#(I)+M#(I)

' Check 4 X Over Screen Limits....

If X#(I)>320
X#(I)=X#(I)-320
End If
If X#(I)<0
X#(I)=320+X#(I)
End If

' Check And C if Snow Has Landed...

If Y#(I)+YV>YM-H(X#(I))

' See How High the snow is below the new Flake...

If H(X#(I))>Rnd(4)+2
XV=Rnd(2)-1
X#(I)=X#(I)+XV
End If

' The Dead SnowFlake...

F Plot X#(I),YM-H(X#(I)),Z(I)

' Reset SnowFlake

H(X#(I))=H(X#(I))+1
KEY#(I)=0
X#(I)=Rnd(320)
Y#(I)=0

Else
' Plot if SnowFlake in Air...

Y#(I)=Y#(I)+YV
F Plot X#(I),Y#(I),Z(I)

End If
Else

' Randomability Variable That a SnowFlake will Fall...

KEY#(I)=Rnd(1000)

End If
Next I
Loop

Bye!!!!!!!

DMA... Its all in the Bitplanes! 4 graphics Ne wa

Wed Sep 2, 1998 10:26 am
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


DMA Can Be usefull but it also can be slow.... say for instance u wanted 2 Use a
tint effect in a game or something... Okay sure U could Use point.... read in
all the pixels... then change their colour accordingly 2 the tinted colours in
your pallete! Then again you must have a vastly Excellerated Computer!!!!!!! So
Instead U could Use DMA.... If U know how Screens and Bitplanes work its easy
from here.....

Screens work by layers of bits... take a 64 colour screen... it has 6 bitplanes
2 keep under control...
this is why the more colours U have when doin graphics the slower things can
be.... All of the first 4 bits, if they all =1 then the number produced from
11110 is 31 meaning colour 31... so if U turn the last bit 2 a one U are infact
adding 32 2 the original 31 coz Binary works like this

1 2 4 8 16 32 64 128 256
1 1 1 1 1  0

Col=1+2+4+8+16
Col=31

and what happens if u add 32 to a number lower than 32 in a EHB palette? Any
guesses!!!
You change the colour 2 Half Brite....
So if U were 2 make a prog 2 just change the bits at bitplane 5 on a 64 colour
screen you would get darkening effects.....

But just wait till u use it with 256 cols on a public screen!! HEY HEY! Thats
fun!
Here is a bit of code 2 change the bits on a screen from your coords.....
Don't Let anything go out side the confines of You screen especially on the Y
axis
coz what You R seeing is memory on your screen so if You poke past the set
memory 4 Your screen U R likeley to crash!!!!
Use a clipping procedure or like i have 4 the mouse.
Limit Mouse 128,42 To 320+127,255+41
L0=Logbase(0) ;This can change depends on
what U want 2 do!
Do
MX=X Screen(X Mouse)
MY=Y Screen(Y Mouse)
PX=MX/8
AX=MX-(PX*8)
Bset(7-AX),L0+(MY*40)+PX ;All ways make sure that
L0 is at a logbase though..
Loop

You could also use copy or fill on the screen 2 get large chunks of Bitplanes
changed.....
Also if You want shapes just open another screen with 2 colours ( 1 bitplane )
draw the shape then grab that pitplane and paste it 2 where U want.. or U could
Use a BOB system!

Re: Hard drive.

Thu Jan 1, 1970 7:59 am
(Keith Hill) <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


To the one known as Phil,
> > Urk, I invalidated my hard drive today, and have currently BARELY got
> > it back. The backup routines aren't working, and it is ridiculously
> > fragile.
> > This is a public service announcement:
> > Make a backup now !
> > Anyone got any good disk tools that work with AFS ?
> I'm sorry to say, that your root of your problm is probally due to , the
> nasty AFS system you use :/ I have heard of many a person on IRC sursing
> beacuse they have lost thier data, beacuse 'Of THE DAM AFS SYSTEM, CURCE

I invalidated my hard drive EVERY DAY with FFS, AFS, well, it's twice a
year, and you can almost always get yer files back quickly. Trouble is,
when it breaks, it breaks hard. Quarterback won't back it up at the mo.
In a few days (next time I see my friend with a few spare gig on the drive)
I'll be copying the whole partition over, reformat, and back again.

> YOU!', I don't know of any way to get your data back, the only thing i can
> suggest, is you grit and bear the problrm, and instakll FFS (fast File
> System) the amiga's defualt drriver, it is a lot, better, I have un
> validated my Hard drive Countless times (about 50 off the top of my head)
> and I have all ways got all the data back off my Hard drive, using disksalv,
> I also suggest that you install Disksafe (search aminet for 'disksafe') this
> program captures the harddrive's bitamp (or something) and helps stopping
> the drive getting invalidated, since i installed it , i have only hafd to
> use disksalv 1'nce , and that onyl 1 time, not the usal 3 , no fun with a
> 1.2 gig hd :/

Interesting. Not familiar with that proggie. I never got on well with ffs.
Slow, nasty. At the mo, I have some of my drives AFS, and some FFS. It works,
and I hardly ever (twice a year !) get problems with any of the drives, and
I have an almost complete backup on other partitions. Unfortunately, the backup
suddenly failed for no good reason this time (it says the archive is corrupt
when it validates it) so I'm stuck with the data in the mess it is. At least
I bypassed the problem. AFS has the lovely :.deldir, and the lovely
removedirentry program, which are lifesavers.

FFS really did invalidate like every day. I was spending two hours loading the
machine on a regular basis, and running disksalv (or qbtools) every week or so
for a day and a half. AFS really helps.

I'd say FFS is more software recoverable, and MUCH more prone to problems, but
AFS has fewer problems, and the data is practically ALWAYS copy-recoverable.
I want a disksalv proggie for AFS.

Challenge for AmosPro Programmers...

Thu Sep 3, 1998 12:30 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

I have a challenge for any AmosPro programmer, I am currently writing
an RPG based on ChronoTrigger, (I may need beta testers for it after I
sort it out propperly) and I have developed a full screen map scrolling
routine. The only problem is, its not very good: Because AMOS seems to
update screen offsets 1 vbl after screen swaps the bob updates became
unsynced so my routine has to waste a VBL to fix this problem. It also
has various other problems in it and its messy and slow.

I'd be happy if someone could write:

A map scrolling routine for 16 colour 16x16 icons in a display
288x160 32 colours (the screen can be any size)
It must be able to display 32 colour bobs.
It must be able to handel tile animation.
It must be as fast or faster then my own (mine can go at full 25fps
even with a bit of tile animation). Preferably running at 50fps based on
hardware scrolling although if you could get software scrolling at a
good speed...

I have the AmosTurbo extention, and you can use ASM procedures, DMA
etc.

If no-one wants to write one of these off the top of there heads (I
took me a while for me to sort mine out) then I could rip mine from my
sorce and post it so someone can optimise it.

I'd be greatful if someone did manage this for me ;)

See ya

	Message #832 of 8180

Re: pbrowne

Thu Sep 3, 1998 1:42 am
<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


>>I've written some various garbage programs (some useful, most just
trivial

>> experiments) - nothing really worth noting (anybody need a Hexagon
drawing

>> routine? or another AD&D character generator? - didn't think so :)
>> My first (and really ONLY) attempt at writing a game was some years ago,
>> making use of the TOME extension. >
>> Phil,

> What kind of game were you attempting to make?
> Ken

Well, if you can cast your mind back to the days when the Commodore 64
ruled, you may remember a game named R.O.B.B. (Raid Over Bungling(?) Bay) -
a simple yet fun helicoptor game. The view is from above the chopper, and
it basically rotates in the centre of the screen while the ground below
scrolls beneath you (in many directions). Lots of jets trying to shoot you
down, and patrol boats, guns, etc...

I was trying to make an AMOS/Amiga version of this. Having never really
attempted to code a game before, it was quite fun and challenging. I got
the helicoptor flying about the screen, shooting stuff, and I used TOME to
scroll the background. Unfortunately, this last part failed miserably -
the scrolling was REAL slow and had some other nasty bugs. And for
whatever reason, I left this project on the back burner and have only
really gotten back to it lately - which is when I found that my version of
TOME didn't like AMOSPRO.

I'd like to give this another shot.

Phil 8-)

	Message #836 of 8180

Amos to DirectX (slightly off-topic)

Wed Sep 2, 1998 2:25 am
Andy H <geosync@ozemail.com.au>


Hi all,

I don`t want to come out sounding like a smug bastard or a Microsoft
supporter, but I've been learning DirectX code and I believe it is
encouraging news for us AMOSers.
I`ve got this book 'Windows Game Programming For Dummies' by Andre
LaMothe, and it's a gem. Andre used to write Amiga games and it shows
in his code. Using DirectX w/ VC++, he has recreated much of AMOS
functionality but on a IBM platform.
I thought this DirectX stuff was going to be difficult and I found it
can be quite easy. Admittedly it's a bit of a grind to wade through
complexities of COM and methods for DirectX, but once you have read that
bit, the rest becomes a breeze.
This is starting to become a book review....Anyway my main point is,
using DirectX, us guys can get our Amiga games onto multiple platforms
with a bit of study of DirectX. I know it's defeating the purpose of
defending the Amiga and AMOS but wouldn`t you like more people to check
out your games? The new Sega console supports DirectX so you could
theoretically get you game onto that too.
FOOD FOR THOUGHT ANYHOO...
Andy H.

BOBs & bit-planes

Thu Sep 3, 1998 11:05 am
Ömer ÖZYILDIRIM <km97y019@students.itu.edu.tr>


Hi there
I have problems about bobs such as:

- Suppose I have a bob with only 1 bitplane (2 colors). How can I
get AMOS to display it with different colors on a screen with 4 bitplanes
(16 colors). That is I will use only one bob instead of 15 for all color
combinations and it will be only one bit deep instead of 4 resulting a
1/60 of the data size.

- Relating the previous problem, suppose I have a 32 color screen
& 16 color bobs. How can I get AMOS to display bobs with alternating 16
color of the palette (i.e. 0~15 and 16~31)?

These sound like to be solved with PLANE ON/OFF & PLANE PICK
parameters I found in AMIGA's font structure plus bit-shifting during the
blitting process. BUT I really don't know how to get AMOS accomplish these
tasks. May be minterms or something or an extension.

PLUS I need to combine two BOB banks during loading into a
program. Suppose I have N bob banks to be merged in my program which I
will load in pairs. Otherwise I'll have to combine the banks in the bank
editor and have N*N bob banks resulting in a bizzare size of data!


If ayone has the answers please let me know. By the way I had to
give up my AMOS 3D project due to the lack of a good obj editor or a
converter which would be an AMOS Tekken clone.

Thanks.

Omer <km97y019@students.itu.edu.tr>

Re: BOBs & bit-planes

Thu Sep 3, 1998 10:59 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

Well, I don't know exactly how you'd do it, but I've got a pritty good
idea how it'd work (I cant remember the right commands)

> - Suppose I have a bob with only 1 bitplane (2 colors). How can I
> get AMOS to display it with different colors on a screen with 4
bitplanes
> (16 colors). That is I will use only one bob instead of 15 for all
color
> combinations and it will be only one bit deep instead of 4 resulting a
> 1/60 of the data size.

You'd have to set the bob mode/mask so that you could select which
bitplanes the bob should display. I think you'd have to convert it to a
16 colour bob and colour it colour 15 so that the original used all of
the bitplanes, then you could disable the ones you don't want. (I think)

> - Relating the previous problem, suppose I have a 32 color screen
> & 16 color bobs. How can I get AMOS to display bobs with alternating
16
> color of the palette (i.e. 0~15 and 16~31)?

What you'd have to do is create a copy of all the frames of that
bob, making a 32 colour bob that is completely colour 31 (like a mask)
and then draw that bob directly over your 16 colour bob, and set the
masking bobs bitplane to only use bit 5.

> These sound like to be solved with PLANE ON/OFF & PLANE PICK
> parameters I found in AMIGA's font structure plus bit-shifting during
the
> blitting process. BUT I really don't know how to get AMOS accomplish
these
> tasks. May be minterms or something or an extension.

I can't remember which command to set bobs bitplanes, but I know it can
be done with no extentions (I've seen it in an old AMOS demo)

> PLUS I need to combine two BOB banks during loading into a
> program. Suppose I have N bob banks to be merged in my program which I
> will load in pairs. Otherwise I'll have to combine the banks in the
bank
> editor and have N*N bob banks resulting in a bizzare size of data!

I can't help you with this one I'm afraid because I don't use Bob banks,
I've got my own system of loading bobs using IFF screens. If anyone
wants to know how then I can distribute the routines source.

> If ayone has the answers please let me know. By the way I had to

> give up my AMOS 3D project due to the lack of a good obj editor or a
> converter which would be an AMOS Tekken clone.

I know, its crap isn't it. And if you'r thinking of tekken, foret it
with the current Amos3D as it has no real support for animation, It was
hard enough animation a simple 4 frame character.

> Thanks.

> Omer <km97y019@students.itu.edu.tr>

Fri Sep 4, 1998 12:35 am
<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


>From: Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>

>>>> I just recently wrote the beginnings of a Compact Disc Catalogue
program,
>>>> with the emphasis on it being able to write out a random access file
in
>>>> alphabetic/numeric order. The user would input a name of the CD and
some
>>>> other details and that data would then be inserted into the file at
the

>>>> This, I think, could be easily adapted for your Dictionary idea.
>>>> If this is at all interesting to you (or anyone else), I will post the

>>>> to this list. It's not pretty, but it DOES work.

>Yes please!!!

Ok! Here it is, for what it's worth.

As I said, it's not the prettiest code in the world, but it's fairly simple
and should be adaptable.

If you have any questions, don't hesitate to ask.

Phil 8-)

___________________________________________


'
' ** CD Data Storage Attempt **
' (c) 1998 Phil Browne
'
Set Buffer 200
Screen Open 0,640,256,16,Hires
Global RECORDS,NAME$,LF$
Dir$="RAM:"
Open Random 1,"CDList.data"
Field 1,25 As NAME$,1 As LF$
If Exist("CDList.data")
L_O_F
End If
LF$=Chr$(10) : Rem * This puts a Line Feed at the end - so I can read the
file!
Do
Input "Enter Artist Name: ";NAME$
If Upper$(NAME$)="EXIT" Then Exit
INSERT
Loop
Close 1
Edit
'
Procedure L_O_F
' ** Determine Length of Random Access File (There has to be a better
way!)
On Error Proc DUMMY
Resume Label HERE
RECORDS=0
Do
Get 1,RECORDS+1
Inc RECORDS
Loop
HERE:
On Error
End Proc
Procedure INSERT
TNAME$=NAME$
If RECORDS>0
For XX=RECORDS To 1 Step -1
Get 1,XX
If Upper$(TNAME$)>Upper$(NAME$)
NAME$=TNAME$
Put 1,XX+1
Exit
Else
Put 1,XX+1
If XX=1
NAME$=TNAME$
Put 1,1
End If
End If
Next XX
Else
Put 1,1
End If
Inc RECORDS
End Proc
Procedure DUMMY
Resume Label
End Proc


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


>On 03-Sep-98, pbrowne@qantas.com.au wrote:
>p> My biggest project was a Solar System generator program (taken directly
>p> from the old Sci-Fi RPG "Universe" - I like "computerising" things like
>p> this.) I was going to incorporate this into some Game/Utility - but as
>p> usual, never quite got there. Maybe one day...!
>How does it works? Is it a simulation of a generation of a solar system or
>just program which makes some realistic solar systems, like e.g. in
>Frontier and so?

The quick answer is that it makes realistic solar systems.

In "Universe" there was a complex, fairly thorough method of creating solar
systems that could be visited by the players in that RPG. First you pick a
star (type) and then determine such things as number of planets, moons for
each planet and asteroid belts. Then for each planet and moon AND asteroid
belt, you determine other things like size of the planetoid, temperature
and etc. Each planet is broken down into segments (as little as one for a
small moon through to fifty or so for big planets) and the terrain for
these segments is then determined.

What I've written is a pretty big program that does all the above plus
draws the planets (when selected) and gives some details on them. I guess
it's about 80% complete. What I wanted to do was draw continents and etc
on the planets, based on the terrain for each segment. I never could quite
work out a way to do that, though. (What is drawn is a planet with lots of
ringed segments filled with a certain terrain "picture" - the end result
doesn't look at all real, but it does convey the general nature of the
area).

Other things like civilization level, population, etc have not yet been
coded (in the game, it was up to the GM to determine such things, often
based on proximity of the solar system to Sol (the centre of of the
civilized Universe in this case).

The program (like many of my programs, in fact) needs a decent interface.
Not very user friendly, I guess. :)

Phil 8-)

Re: Amos MED bugs

"Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>


On 04-Sep-98, Infinity wrote:
> How do I prevent Amos Pro 2 stopping MED music when new banks are loaded?

You can use an extension - this ALWAYS happens with the AMOS Music Ext. What
you CAN do, however, is to do some tricks with loading it as a binary file and
then convince AMOS that it is a MED file. I can't remember exactly how, but I
have done it this way.

> How do I prevent Amos Pro 2 samples repeating forever if MED music has been
played by anything that session?

There definetly IS a solution to this, although I can't remember it.

hey folks,
alot of your mail is coming to me in two parts, one a text file
and one an HTML formatted file. I use Pine for unix which will let me
view the text part but it takes a few steps and is a pain. The html file
is identical to the text file and I think some of you with HTML or WEB
based email services are getting your mail sent as both plain text and
HTML. I find it a slight hassle to deal with but not that bad, still if
you didn't realize this was happenign you may want to check the settings
on your email service.

Thanks,
Scott Matott sXe

Hi,

Another big message :).... please read it, and talk about its contents.

Very well... a lot of good things are now moving.... first the new Amos
Factory site. Now AMOS has is real home! ALL the Amos world is here, news,
programs, infos and much more... a *BIG* thank you to Rune J. Keller for the
excellent site design!

We're are working hard in order to support the Amos community, but now you've
to support us! So, send us immediatelly infos about your projects! Game,
utilities, misc programs, everythings you're coding in Amos is of our (your)
interest... *The AMOS Factory projects page is waiting you!* Increase your
programs interest by publishing them on our site!!* now! *Very, very
important...

Your ICQ uin isn't listed in the developers page? Doh! Send it
immediatelly....

The main AMOS support resources are now ready and working:

- the official AMOS site - The Amos Factory (http://www.seta.it/amos/)
- the new official AMOS PD Library - (http://www.mushy-pd.demon.co.uk)
- the new great mailing-list (Thanks Michael Cox!)
- the upcoming GNU Amos Distillery (see belove)
- AmosZine is coming back!!

But i want even more! :) There are again a lot of AMOS users who doesn't
know our site, the mailing list, the development work and so on..... we need
local support!!! So.. we've created the headquarter, now we need the local
branch of our factory :) The AMOS clubs must be opened again!

If someone is interested in this project, please contact me. I'm searching the
local coordinators for the several countries! Now you'll not be alone, but
thanks to internet you'll a member of our great family.

Other projects are under construction... now i want spent some words about
the *GNU Amos Distillery.* What is it? oh well.... this is my dream! Probably
you've heard something about the Free Software or GNU programs.... please
visit now the Free Software Foundation at http://www.fsf.org, you'll find tons
of infos about this great concept!!!

The GNU Amos Distillery will be the support site for GNU Amos projects... i
strongly belive in the Free Software power, and the site will share this power
with all the amos community!

``Free software'' refers to the users' freedom to run, copy, distribute,
study, change and improve the software. More precisely, it refers to three
levels of freedom:

The freedom to study how the program works and adapt it to your needs.
The freedom to redistribute copies so you can share with your neighbor.
The freedom to improve the program, and release your improvements to the
public, so that the whole community benefits.

A Free program is updated 10 time faster then a commercial one!

Several attempt to create mailing-list projects has been made in the past
period.... in the near future you'll have the oppurtunity to make them a
reality using the Free Software formula! Several famous projects are available
as Free Software.. one name: Lynux!

Please visit the Free Software Foundation site! This project will let us to
produce good quality software, and show to the other the real amos (.. and its
community) capabilities!


_*Anyway YOU are the succesfull key of our projects! without YOUR support*_
_*our efforts are vanished!*_

extension.. this is the /demo/ version of the commercial version released some
time ago by Quartz Informatique (France). *ATTENTION:* it doens't reflect the
actual status of the extension! Now it's bigger (90k! this is 47k!), easier
and powerfull! anyway it give you a clear idea about its capabilities! Enjoy!

A little GUI Extension V2 demo program will be also available for testing....
so you can see in action some new features! ;)

--

	Message #886 of 8183

LHA Trashing

Fri Sep 4, 1998 1:20 am
Andy H <geosync@ozemail.com.au>


Hi all,

On the subject of LHA's being corrupted, I have found that some servers
don`t recognize the LHA suffix and treat it as some sort of unspecific
binary file (ergo goodbye LHA). The easiest way to stop this from
happening is to archive as usual using LHA but rename it to #?.ZIP when
sending it over the Internet. Most servers respect the archive
structure of the IBM ZIP file and wont tamper with it. When the user
recieves the "fake" ZIP file they can simply rename it and unpack with
LHA.

Andy H.

	Message #897 of 8183

REPOSTING OF JOYSTICK CODE...

Sat Sep 5, 1998 3:47 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


ORIGINALLY SENT WEDNESDAY, NOW I AM RESENDING...
----------

>>> Hey! Look! At this Ne1 want a piece of joystick code...
>>Timer=0
>>For A=0 To 100000
>> J=Joy(1) : K=J-2 : P#=J/4.0 : P=P# : I=Sgn(J)
>> If P#=P Then X=Sgn(J-6)*I
>> If P=0 Then Y=I*(K+K+1)
>>Next
>>Print Timer

>> Hmm this seemed a bit too complicated, so I decided to check it out
>>(and I managed to kill 5mins at the same time ;)
>>Timer=0
>>For A=0 To 100000
>> X=0 : Y=0
>> If Jup(1) Then Y=-1
>> If Jdown(1) Then Y=1
>> If Jleft(1) Then X=-1
>> If Jright(1) Then X=1
>>Next
>>Print Timer

Well, I live for writing compact, optimized code...
THE OPTIMIZED WAY:
Timer=0
For REP=0 To 100000
X=Jleft(1)-Jright(1)
Y=Jup(1)-Jdown(1)
Next REP
Print Timer

Compiled with AMOS PRO Compiler and tested on a 14MHz NTSC
Amiga...

NO JOYSTICK MOVEMENT
First version: 779
Second version: 502
My version: 471

HOLDING DOWN ON JOYSTICK
First Version: 933
Second version: 511
My version: 476

Obviously, if tested on an accelerated Amiga the performance will be
greatly increased (ie. smaller times) and it is much shorter as well.


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

oh by the way... if u want it 2 go faster use variables instead of the 1's
it most probably wont make a difference for a single digit.. but it takes
longer 2 read in any numbers and work out there values that it does 2 read a
variable.. thats why it is faster 2 open a screen if u write
Screen open 0,640,256,16,Hires
instead of....
Screen open 0,640,256,16,32768
as Hires is an internal variable!

---START OF PROG---
Input "What Detail (1-200) ?";SKL
ST:
Trap Load Iff "3d/worldmap.lores",0
If Errtrap : Dir$="work:amospro/" : Goto ST : End If
Load Iff "3d/worldmap.lores",1
Screen 0
Cls 0
Degree
'Double Buffer
Autoback 0
PX=160
PY=100
Screen To Front 0
MX=320/SKL

ZOM=2
Do
Timer=0
ROTATE[ANG,ZOM,MX,MY,PX,PY,SKL]

Print At(0,0);"VBL:";T#-1;" ","FPS:";50/T#;" "

'If Jleft(1)
' ANG=ANG+10
'End If
'If Jright(1)
' ANG=ANG-10
'End If
''Bell

Procedure ROTATE[ANG,ZOM,MX,MY,PX,PY,SKL]
MX2=MX/2
MY2=MY/2
ZOM=ZOM*SKL
'ZOM#=ZOM#/64
S=Sin(ANG)*256
C=Cos(ANG)*256
For Y=0 To MY
'BY=(Y^2)/(128/skl)
For X=0 To MX
XM=(X-MX2)*ZOM
YM=(Y-MY2)*ZOM
'OX=XM*C+YM*S+Rnd(16384)
'OY=YM*C-XM*S+Rnd(16384)
Rem /\ Use these if you want a smoother finnish /\
Rem Its slower then \/ those though!
OX=XM*C+YM*S
OY=YM*C-XM*S
OX=OX/16384 : OY=OY/16384
Screen 1
P= 0t0,0,0(OX+PX,OY+PY) - This line has Gone weird!!!
If P>-1
Screen 0
Trap Ed X*SKL,Y*SKL,P - And this line!
'If SKL>1
'F Plot X*SKL+1,Y*SKL+1,1
'End If
End If
'Trap F Plot X*SKL,Y*SKL/2+50+BY,P
'Ink P : Bar X*SKL,Y*SKL To X*SKL+SKL,Y*SKL+SKL
Next
Next
End Proc

Hey Andrew Crowe!

Sun Sep 6, 1998 10:10 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Thankyou 4 the code... I think i can use it and put it 2 use in my isometric 3d
engine!!!
Here is a Optimized version of your code that i did so it would fit with my
code!
Thanx... Phil!

' Phil Glanville - sNaKeByTe SoFtWaRe!

-Start of Code-
' I have Speeded up the code as much as I can by optimization!
' I think I can use this! Thankyou... I thought U would want
' The faster code... so here You are!
' I have turned all numbers within the main loop 2 variables
' as it is faster... but I think it makes it slower when compiled
' so if U compile this Reenter the numbers instead of the varialbes!
' Ps... I do have the Turbo Extension its just that I think the File
' Got scrambled while being emailed! I actually managed 2 guess what
' the commands where ( coz of their Syntax ) after I sent U the 2nd mail
' But I wasn't sure.... I've sped up the prog by not using point...
' instead by reading the Image data from a bank... Memory Extensive
' but faster!!!!
' Bye!

Input "What Detail (1-200) ?";SKL
Load Iff "3d/worldmap.lores",0
Flash Off
Curs Off
Degree
Cls 0
ST8=Start(8)
Double Buffer
Autoback 0
SW=320
SH=200
MX=320/SKL
MY=200/SKL
PX=160
PY=100
ZOM=50
D2=2
NU=256
UN=16384
AA=10
ZA=4
Do
If OANG<>ANG or ZOM<>OZOM
MX2=MX/D2
MY2=MY/D2
ZIM=ZOM*SKL
S=Sin(ANG)*NU
C=Cos(ANG)*NU
For Y=0 To MY
For X=0 To MX
XM=(X-MX2)*ZIM
YM=(Y-MY2)*ZIM
OX=XM*C+YM*S
OY=YM*C-XM*S
NX=OX/UN+PX
NY=OY/UN+PY
If NX>SW or NX<0 or NY>SH or NY<0
P=0
Else
P=Peek(ST8+(NY*SW)+NX)
End If
Cls P,X*SKL,Y*SKL To X*SKL+SKL,Y*SKL+SKL
Next X
Next Y
Screen Swap
End If
OANG=ANG
OZOM=ZOM
JA=Jleft(1)+-Jright(1)
JB=Jup(1)+-Jdown(1)
ANG=ANG+(JA*AA)
ZOM=ZOM+(JB*ZA)
Loop
-End-

	Message #921 of 8183

Rotating Stuff

Mon Sep 7, 1998 2:47 am
<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


Hi again AMOS people,

In regards to those people Rotating graphics, I have just recently started
yet another little project (maybe I should just call it a "challenge", that
way if I don't actually finish it I won't be disappointed! - I can say I
satisfied the challenge rather than stopped the project).

Anyway, my challenge was to make an object made of a series of (x,y)
co-ordinates, joined together by Draw commands and then Rotate that object
about a nominated point (central to the object, naturally - or close to
it). The points (x,y)'s would be recalculated and then Draw(n) together
again.

Not quite so complex as rotating a full colour graphic object, but all I
wanted was to emulate an old Star Trek game I played once or twice MANY
years ago. It was a two player game, each player controlling a Starship
that flitted about a screen with a Star in the centre acting as a gravity
well.

It's probably been done (and easily a lot better than what I'll come up
with) - but what the heck! :)

And yes, I could just as easily draw the object in a paint program, rotate
it a few degrees many times over and make those little piccies into a
sprite... but where's the fun in that!?!

Phil 8-)

	Message #923 of 8183

I got Isometric! Andrew Crowe!

Mon Sep 7, 1998 9:35 am
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Thankyou! I have now made my Isometric rotate program! Here it is! I though U
might like 2 See it... Its mainly your program! but I have added bits I know and
have tried before and also optimised it 4 the purpose I want... So it doesn't
have zoom! (ZOM?) and other stuff!
Any way here it is and Thanx!
Bye!
Any Ideas how to make it go faster?

Load Iff "Hd2:Vector/3d/worldmap.lores",1
Load Iff "Hd2:Vector/3d/worldmap.lores",0
Flash Off
Curs Off
Degree
Cls 0
Double Buffer
Autoback 0
SW=64
SH=64
MX=SW/2
MY=SH/2
GNA=-1
NU=256
UN=400
PRE=4
AA=10
ZA=5

Do
If GNA<>ANG
Blit Clear -1
S=Sin(ANG)*NU
C=Cos(ANG)*NU
For Y=0 To SW Step PRE
For X=0 To SH Step PRE
Screen 1
Trap P=F Point(X+MX,Y+MY)
RX=X-MX
RY=Y-MY
NX=(RX*C+RY*S)/UN+MX
NY=((RY*C-RX*S)/UN+MY)/2
Screen 0
Cls P,NX,NY To NX+PRE,NY+PRE
Next X
Next Y
Screen Swap
End If
GNA=ANG
JA=Jleft(1)+-Jright(1)
ANG=ANG+(JA*AA)
Loop

Re: LHA Trashing

Mon Sep 7, 1998 11:24 am
TigerGutt <warewulf@geocities.com>


I think this is due to the fact that netscape trashed the <cr> or
something. The same thing happends to mp3 files.

There is a tool on aminet for fixing this files i think.

Andy H wrote:
>
> From: Andy H <geosync@ozemail.com.au>
>
> Hi all,
>
> On the subject of LHA's being corrupted, I have found that some servers
> don`t recognize the LHA suffix and treat it as some sort of unspecific
> binary file (ergo goodbye LHA). The easiest way to stop this from
> happening is to archive as usual using LHA but rename it to #?.ZIP when
> sending it over the Internet. Most servers respect the archive
> structure of the IBM ZIP file and wont tamper with it. When the user
> recieves the "fake" ZIP file they can simply rename it and unpack with
> LHA.
>
> Andy H.
>
> ------------------------------------------------------------------------
> Help support ONElist, while generating interest in your product or
> service. ONElist has a variety of advertising packages. Visit
> http://www.onelist.com/advert.html for more information.

Re: Rotating Stuff

Mon Sep 7, 1998 2:16 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

On 07-Sep-98, pbrowne@qantas.com.au wrote something which is obviously
worth replying to:

> Anyway, my challenge was to make an object made of a series of (x,y)
> co-ordinates, joined together by Draw commands and then Rotate that
object
> about a nominated point (central to the object, naturally - or close
to
> it). The points (x,y)'s would be recalculated and then Draw(n)
together
> again.

The easy way to do this is not to store the points in (x,y) but as
(angle from center,distance from center). Then use Sin and Cos to draw
the lines in. To convert an X,Y point you'd have to use trig. functions.
If you give me a little while then I sould be able to make a routine for
you ;)


See ya.

Mon Sep 7, 1998 5:53 pm
Bartek Iwanojko <jirey@friko6.onet.pl>


On 07-09-98, Ives, Neil, IVESNJ wrote:

> 720k PC disk. Someone on the list knows the answer to this problem. Can
you
> help please?
>

It is posible to split any big file to chunks of 720k using eg. NC (you can
also use rar) and transfer them to Amiga using DD disks, you can join them
using system command join (join file1 file2 file3 ... to file) or using very
easy DOpus5 join module (if you will use rar then you can use UnRAR from
AmiNet to unarchive it).

JiRey

	Message #933 of 8183 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Rotating+Zooming line vectors!

Mon Sep 7, 1998 7:07 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

I've now done a program that lets you create and then load/save a
real 2d rotatable+zoomable line vector object using only AMOSTurbo
extention, which is easily converted to standard amos code. (take the F
off 'F draw', 'F plot' etc.)

(The editor is a bit crappy and you can't load into to level editor,
only after you finish in it and go into vector view mode ;)

It could do with some optimisation, but it isn't too slow, I've
included 2 example objects:

A Starship Enterprise, an XMas_Tree , a simpler Enterprise and a simple
object.

The Enterprise and XMas_Tree updates at 25fps after compilation and the
simpler ones
updates at full speed (50 fps) on my 25mhz 040 ami ;)



Please feel free to optimise/use this code in your games, but I'd like
to see the end result please ;)



See ya.
--

Re: Rotating+Zooming line vectors!

Tue Sep 8, 1998 12:11 am
<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


>Hi Everybody,
> I've now done a program that lets you create and then load/save a
>real 2d rotatable+zoomable line vector object using only AMOSTurbo
>extention, which is easily converted to standard amos code. (take the F
>off 'F draw', 'F plot' etc.)
> (The editor is a bit crappy and you can't load into to level editor,
>only after you finish in it and go into vector view mode ;)
> It could do with some optimisation, but it isn't too slow, I've
>included 2 example objects:
>A Starship Enterprise, an XMas_Tree , a simpler Enterprise and a simple
>object.
>The Enterprise and XMas_Tree updates at 25fps after compilation and the
>simpler ones
>updates at full speed (50 fps) on my 25mhz 040 ami ;)
>Please feel free to optimise/use this code in your games, but I'd like
>to see the end result please ;)

	Message #956 of 8185

What about Vumeters?

Tue Sep 8, 1998 8:46 am
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Has any one out there got any iteresting ideas for vumeters... here is a
little prog i was mucking around with this morning... note that this is a
rubbish prog ... And there is no need to run a speed check on it or even
optimize it as it is only an idea...its just I've never really used Vumeters
before.. so
i was just looking....

!start of code!
Screen Open 0,320,256,16,0
Flash Off
Curs Off
Blit Clear -1
ST:
F$=Fsel$("")
If F$<>""
Track Load F$,6
Else
Goto ST
End If
Track Play 6
Double Buffer
Autoback 0
Do
NV0=Vumeter(1)
NV1=Vumeter(2)
NV2=Vumeter(3)
If NV0>V0
V0=NV0
End If
If NV1>V1
V1=NV1
End If
If NV2>V2
V2=NV2
End If
If V0>1
V0=V0-2
End If
If V1>1
V1=V1-2
End If
If V2>1
V2=V2-2
End If
RCOL=V0/3
GCOL=V1/3
BCOL=V2/3
If RCOL>15
RCOL=15
End If
If GCOL>15
GCOL=15
End If
If BCOL>15
BCOL=15
End If
D#=1.5
NRCL=RCOL/D#
NGCL=GCOL/D#
NBCL=BCOL/D#
Colour 3,BCOL*256+GCOL*16+RCOL
Colour 4,GCOL*256+BCOL*16+RCOL
Colour 5,RCOL*256+GCOL*16+BCOL
Colour 6,NBCL*256+NGCL*16+NRCL
Colour 7,NGCL*256+NBCL*16+NRCL
Colour 8,NRCL*256+NGCL*16+NBCL
RCOL=RCOL+5
GCOL=GCOL+5
BCOL=BCOL+5
If RCOL>15
RCOL=15
End If
If GCOL>15
GCOL=15
End If
If BCOL>15
BCOL=15
End If
Colour 9,BCOL*256+GCOL*16+RCOL
Colour 10,GCOL*256+BCOL*16+RCOL
Colour 11,RCOL*256+GCOL*16+BCOL
If V0<>0
Ink 3
Bar 100,100-V0 To 110,100
End If
If V1<>0
Ink 4
Bar 115,100-V1 To 125,100
End If
If V2<>0
Ink 5
Bar 130,100-V2 To 140,100
End If
Ink 0
Bar 100,0 To 110,100-(V0)
Bar 115,0 To 125,100-(V1)
Bar 130,0 To 140,100-(V2)
Ink 6
F Draw 100,100 To 110,100
F Draw 110,100 To 110,100-V0
Ink 7
F Draw 115,100 To 125,100
F Draw 125,100 To 125,100-V1
Ink 8
F Draw 130,100 To 140,100
F Draw 140,100 To 140,100-V2
Ink 9
F Draw 100,100-V0 To 110,100-V0
F Draw 100,100-V0 To 100,100
Ink 10
F Draw 115,100-V1 To 125,100-V1
F Draw 115,100-V1 To 115,100
Ink 11
F Draw 130,100-V2 To 140,100-V2
F Draw 130,100-V2 To 130,100
Screen Swap
Wait Vbl
Loop

!end of code!

Bye!
Ps if you have amcaf you have faster Vu commands!

	Message #969 of 8185

Bobs and Bit planes!!!!

Tue Sep 8, 1998 8:00 pm
"John Glanville" <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>


Hey there... this prog i have just dug up from my amos drawers tints an
image using bobs!
Using the Plane control in the command....
Bob bob#,background,Planes,Miniterm...
By only changing the bits on a certian Bitplane of a screen you can produce
a tint effect if your palette is set up properley...
You should set up the palette like so....
colours 00 - 07 is the normal palette of the image...
colours 08 - 15 is all the above 00 - 07 colours tinted to a colour... say
blue!
colours 16 - 23 is the 00 - 07 colours tinted another colour.... say red!
colours 24 - 32 is the 00 - 07 colours tinted a mix between blue and red..
purple!

Just if you didn't know! Sorry if you already new that but there are people
out there that don't and I know how annoying it is to not know how to do
something!

The program is attached and in asc. if you download the attach you will have
my test image stored in bank 8... the asc doesn't!

Prog start!
Screen Open 0,320,256,64,Lowres
Flash Off
Curs Off
Cls 0
Ink 63
F Circle 20,20,20,63
Paint 20,20
Get Bob 0,1,0,0 To 40,45
Cls 0
Load Iff "Hd2:testbob.ilbm",0
Double Buffer
Autoback 0
Set Bob 1,0,8,
Set Bob 2,0,16,
A0#=0.3
A1#=0.2
X1#=320
CX=200
CY=100
MS0=5
MS1=6
MS2=4
MS3=7
Repeat
CX=X Screen(X Mouse)
CY=Y Screen(Y Mouse)
If X0#>CX
If S0#<MS0
S0#=S0#+A0#
End If
End If
If X0#<CX
If S0#>-MS0
S0#=S0#-A0#
End If
End If
If Y0#>CY
If S1#<MS1
S1#=S1#+A0#
End If
End If
If Y0#<CY
If S1#>-MS1
S1#=S1#-A0#
End If
End If
If X1#>CX
If S2#<MS2
S2#=S2#+A1#
End If
End If
If X1#<CX
If S2#>-MS2
S2#=S2#-A1#
End If
End If
If Y1#>CY
If S3#<MS3
S3#=S3#+A1#
End If
End If
If Y1#<CY
If S3#>-MS3
S3#=S3#-A1#
End If
End If
X0#=X0#-S0#
Y0#=Y0#-S1#
X1#=X1#-S2#
Y1#=Y1#-S3#
Bob 1,X0#,Y0#,1
Bob 2,X1#,Y1#,1
Wait Vbl
Until 0

Prog End!


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #970 of 8185 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: virtual mem

Tue Sep 8, 1998 9:10 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

On 09-Sep-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote something which is obviously worth
replying to:
> From: Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>

> Is it possible to use AMOS pro to force the
> computer to use part of hd when rammemory
> is lower than for example 0,5 mb?
See ya.

You can't use *REAL *Virtual memory without an MMU in you processor,
and even if you do, you can't control it in amos propperly. If you set
up your system for virtual memory then AMOS should be able to use it. Of
corce, you don't have to use real vmem. You can buffer things on disk
from your AMOS program as much as you like, that would cover for virtual
memory fine.

uhm, although I havnt done TextureMapping before, I know how to do it
and if you come up with any probs feel free to ask, but I dont have much
time on my hands these days - so if your looking for someone to write a
tmapping routine for you in 68k and just plug it into amos, I dont have
the time to do that as TGE is my MAIN priority, BUT if you like....

If you send me decent amos code with a super slow tmapper I'll
convert it into 68k, however your code must work first.
Also, Im stuck for time these days, I'll need 2 weeks
(max) to convert it.

By 'Decent' AMOS code, I mean *NOT* spagetti code!!!
Goto's i dont mind, but NOTHING even NEARLY like:

A: .....
goto F

B: .....
if x then goto C
gosub E
goto D

C: ....
if y then gosub E
goto A

D: ....
if q or p or r then goto B
goto F

E: .....
if abc<>def then goto C
if def<>x+y then goto D
return

F: gosub E
goto D


I think you get the point ;}
no mumbo jumbo stuff!!!!

cya,

	Message #973 of 8185 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: virtual mem

Tue Sep 8, 1998 6:38 pm
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


On 09-Sep-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
>From: Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>

>Is it possible to use AMOS pro to force the
>computer to use part of hd when rammemory
>is lower than for example 0,5 mb?

no,
and you'ld be best not to try ;}
the reason for using memory is RAM is MUCH MUCH MUCH faster
than reading off HD. IF you want to minamize the ram usage
you should load things as you need them, and the second your
about to load something else free all the other things in mem
or as many as possible!

cya,

Re: BOBs & bit-planes

Wed Sep 9, 1998 3:10 pm
Ömer ÖZYILDIRIM <km97y019@students.itu.edu.tr>


On Thu, 3 Sep 1998, Andrew Crowe wrote:

>
> > - Relating the previous problem, suppose I have a 32 color screen
> > & 16 color bobs. How can I get AMOS to display bobs with alternating
> 16
> > color of the palette (i.e. 0~15 and 16~31)?
>
> What you'd have to do is create a copy of all the frames of that
> bob, making a 32 colour bob that is completely colour 31 (like a mask)
> and then draw that bob directly over your 16 colour bob, and set the
> masking bobs bitplane to only use bit 5.
>
Good idea, but making a copy of all frames with color 31 is
neither easier, nor less memory consuming than making a copy with new
colors. But the previous idea was good really.

>
> > If ayone has the answers please let me know. By the way I had to
> > give up my AMOS 3D project due to the lack of a good obj editor or a
> > converter which would be an AMOS Tekken clone.
>
> I know, its crap isn't it. And if you'r thinking of tekken, foret it
> with the current Amos3D as it has no real support for animation, It was
> hard enough animation a simple 4 frame character.
>

Interlace Bug.

Thu Sep 10, 1998 12:10 am
<pbrowne@qantas.com.au>


Hi again!

Here's a problem I've had so long now that I've forgotten about it (I tend
to work around it or just ignore it) - but seeing how as I now have contact
with many wise AMOS/Amigans, I thought I'd ask for some advice.

The problem is with AMOS and Interlaced screens plus the addition of a
Spectrum/Holobyte graphics card on my A3000.

Before the card, all was fine and dandy. Once the card was installed, the
screens "lost" their "lacing" (now look like blocky lowres screens).

Is this a familiar problem to anyone else?

I seem to remember reading (long ago) that AMOS didn't like (or display)
interlace screens, but introduced it just to prove it could! (and because
people wanted it).

Thanks for any wisdom you can pass on...

Phil 8-)

	Message #1010 of 8185

The culprit...

Thu Sep 10, 1998 6:00 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


Now, here is the culprit which apparently caused all of my trouble.
A simple ASCII source attachment for the snow demo. I mailed this
out a week ago to the guy who requested it, but as I said I would
return with the source, here it is... (included in this e-mail, no more
ASCII attachments as they seem to block my ability to post for
nearly a week)!!


-----<START OF CODE>-----
' *************************************************
'* THE AMOS SNOW DEMO *
'* CREATED BY GARFIELD BENJAMIN SEPTEMBER, 1998 *
' *************************************************
NUMFLKS=25 : Rem the number of snowflakes
Dim SNOWXPOS(NUMFLKS),SNOWYPOS(NUMFLKS)
Dim SNOWYSPD(NUMFLKS)

Rem Define procedures...
Procedure CLEAR_SNOW
Shared NUMFLKS
Shared SNOWXPOS(),SNOWYPOS()
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS-1
Rem where 0=Background color
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP),SNOWYPOS(REP),0
Next REP
End Proc

Procedure SNOW_UPDATE
Shared REALSCRN,TESTSCRN,NUMFLKS
Shared SNOWXPOS(),SNOWYPOS(),SNOWYSPD()
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS-1
XSPD=Rnd(4)-2
TESTXPOS=SNOWXPOS(REP)+XSPD
If(TESTXPOS<0) Then TESTXPOS=0
If(TESTXPOS>319) Then TESTXPOS=319
TESTYPOS=SNOWYPOS(REP)+SNOWYSPD(REP)
Rem We have the new position, now check for collision...
Screen TESTSCRN
TEST=Point(TESTXPOS,TESTYPOS)
Screen REALSCRN
If(TEST<>0) : Rem where 0=Background color
Rem Ahh, the snow has landed!!
Rem Now, find pixel directly above surface...
Screen TESTSCRN
Repeat
Dec TESTYPOS
Until(Point(TESTXPOS,TESTYPOS)=0) : rem 0=back color
Rem mark the collision (TEST) screen...
Plot TESTXPOS,TESTYPOS,SNOWYSPD(REP)+26
Screen REALSCRN
Rem and "land" on the REAL screen...
Plot TESTXPOS,TESTYPOS,SNOWYSPD(REP)+26
Rem So, we reset this snowflake...
SNOWXPOS(REP)=Rnd(352)
SNOWYPOS(REP)=0
SNOWYSPD=Rnd(4)+1
Else
SNOWXPOS(REP)=TESTXPOS
SNOWYPOS(REP)=TESTYPOS
Rem Here, the snow is being plotted in a color based
Rem on YSPD, resulting in a range of colors from
Rem white to a bluish grey. This makes a nice effect
Rem when the snow builds up.
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP),SNOWYPOS(REP),SNOWYSPD(REP)+26
End If
Next REP
End Proc

Rem Initialize the snow...
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS-1
SNOWXPOS(REP)=Rnd(352)
SNOWYPOS(REP)=(REP*3)
SNOWYSPD(REP)=Rnd(4)+1
Next REP

Rem Create two screens...
REALSCRN=0 : TESTSCRN=1
Screen Open REALSCRN,320,240,32,Lowres
Curs Off : Flash Off : Hide : Cls 0
Autoback 0 : Bob Update Off

Screen Open TESTSCRN,320,240,32,Lowres
Curs Off : Flash Off : Hide : Cls 0
Autoback 0 : Bob Update Off : Screen Hide TESTSCRN

Rem Initialize the screen palettes AND/OR load the IFF picture in
Screen REALSCRN
Colour 0,$0 : Rem background
Rem create snow palette...
Colour 27,$78F : Colour 28,$9AF : Colour 29,$BDF
Colour 30,$DEF : Colour 31,$FFF
Rem Draw all your static images into REALSCRN now...
Rem Here, I'm just drawing a bar across the bottom of the screen...
Ink 31 : Bar 0,208 To 319,212
Rem
Screen Copy REALSCRN To TESTSCRN

Rem let it snow, Let It Snow, LET IT SNOW!!
ALL_DONE=False
Timer=0
Repeat
CLEAR_SNOW
SNOW_UPDATE
If Fire(0) Then ALL_DONE=True
If Timer>6000 Then ALL_DONE=True
Wait Vbl
Until ALL_DONE

Fade 5 : Wait 75
End
-----<END OF CODE>-----

Nothing fancy, but it is fully working and should give anyone a good
foundation to build on.


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

non-AMOS: ONElist Status Update

Thu Sep 10, 1998 11:52 am
"Cox, Michael D" <michael.cox@eds.com>


> Status Report for ONElist.com
>
> Over the past several weeks, we have completed our internal upgrades.
> Our
> system will now be able to support our continued growth for a long
> time
> to come, while providing the high level of service we hope you've come
> to
> expect from ONElist.
>
> We have also been able to add several new features, including:
>
> * Multiple Moderators
> Each list can have several moderators. You can add and remove
> moderators
> through the Manage List screen.
> * No Post and No Mail
> Moderators can now disable subscribers' ability to post to lists.
> Also,
> subscribers can temporarily turn off mail delivery.
> * Private Archives
> Lists can now specify that archives are only viewable by
> subscribers.
> * New List Center
> Within the User Center, for each list you are subscribed to, there
> is
> a link to the List Center. The List Center contains links to the
> list archives as well as another new feature, group bookmarks.
> * Group Bookmarks
> Each list now has a Bookmark Center, where subscribers can share
> links
> to web sites.
> * Message Trailers
> List moderators can specify a message to be appended to each
> message
> sent to the list.
> * Unlisted Lists
> List moderators can specify that a list is unlisted, which means it
> will
> not show up in list searches or on the New Lists page.
> * Advanced Search
> Users can now specify a language and/or maturity level when
> searching
> for lists.
> * listname-owner@onelist.com
> Each list now has a special address that will send email to the
> list
> moderators for that list.
> * Adding Users improved
> The Add Users function has been improved. Moderators can now add
> people to their list without the users having to reply to a
> confirmation
> email.
> * Improved Moderator Control
> Moderators can now switch users between normal subscription and
> digest
> subscription, through the Manage List screen.
>
> We are continuing to add new features and improve the ONElist system.
> Our goal is to make ONElist the best possible mailing list community
> system.
> To do that we need your help. How can we make it better? How can we
> make it
> easier to use? What features are missing?
>
> Please email your comments to comments@onelist.com

Re: Rotating+Zooming line vectors!

Thu Sep 10, 1998 7:37 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

On 09-Sep-98, pbrowne@qantas.com.au wrote something which is obviously
worth replying to:
> From: pbrowne@qantas.com.au

> Well, I tried the code that you did supply... and I gotta say, I'm
damn
> impressed!

> I don't normally praise anyone else's code (no one praises mine, so
why
> make a fool of myself?) but your's was enough to make me break with
> tradition!

> My only question for you is the editor - why the "snap-to-grid" like
> functionality? Easier to code or use?


Thanks, Its the first time I've done vector work. The grid in the
editor is to make shapes easier to draw. If you don't like it then you
can adjust it/turn it off with + and - (I can't remember whether I put
those instructions into the sorce).

Anyway, it could still do with improvements - the conversion isn't
100% accurate and sometimes I've seen lines overlap strangely. Its also
a little slow (probably bacause of slow line commands, although
AMOSTurbo shouldn't be that slow.)

Now I hope you can make a decent game with em. You could try doing a
version for filled shapes (using polygon) and write a game like
'Bratwust' (is it called that? I can't remember! ;)

Happy programing ;)

See ya.

Re: Fast texturemapping(?)

Wed Sep 9, 1998 6:56 pm
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


On 09-Sep-98, John Glanville wrote:

>Yes that would be good thanx but i don't know if my prog is atually

uhm, if you are sure its fastest then do it ;oP
either way I dont mind as Im just converting what you give

>To gain speed it has a sort of Fake Chunky system! LOL!
>Not really all it does is instead of ploting single pixels it uses
>blocks... okay so its not great detail but all i want it for is
>walls and floors of an isometric RPG!

I'm not sure about it being interesting to EVERYONE, but I wrote a little
demo-type program that makes use of the Vu meters. What you've got is a
four sided polygon floating randomly about a screen, but each corner jerks
with addition gusto in proportion to a selected sound channel. All to the
sounds of "Smoke on the water"...

Sounds weird? Funny, I called it WEIRD.Amos !

If anyone is at all interested in seeing this "miracle of modern
programming", email me and throw it back at you!

Phil 8-)

	Message #1046 of 8185 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Limit bob fixed!

Fri Sep 11, 1998 11:57 am
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hello Andrew,

On 10-Set-98, Andrew Crowe wrote: [amos-list] Re: mega error with limit bob -
the only workaround -

>
> I've tried every thing, but I've come up with a solution:
>
> Instead of opening a 640x400 I'll open a 640x512 and move all gfx. opps.
> down by 112 pixles. Down the bottom part Limit bob works perfectly. (!?)

hehe :) I've found the bug... i've never noticed it in 7 years!! :)
I've fixed it immediately, and you'll find the update on the Amos Factory site
as
usual ;) Just a moment....

I take the oppurtunity to remember that the Official Amos HomePage address is:

http://www.seta.it/amos/


I've to say that the example program supplied by Andrew Crow is bugged too :),
since he doesn't use the Limit Bob command correctly. i.e:

_CUT_

/Limit Bob 320,0 To 639,200/
/Print " Now if we put a bob on you see it doesn't work!";/
/Box 320,0 To 639,200/
/Bob 1,280,180,1/

Yes is true... it doesn't work, but it's correct! Only the bobs present on the
screen *BEFORE* the limit bob command will be effected. If you put a bob on
the
screen after limit bob it doesn't work. RTFM! :))))


/Print "but if we call different Limit bobs they works fine";/
/Limit Bob 0,0 To 320,200/
/Wait 50/
/Limit Bob 0,200 To 320,400/
/Wait 50/
/Limit Bob 320,200 To 640,400/

Now it works because the bob is already present on the screen......


/Print "But now if we call the original function with the bob"/
/Print "on then it bombs out with 'illegal function call'! "/
/Print /
/Print "Does this happen on your copy? does anyone know why"/
/Print "It gives that error when trying to limit a bob to the upper"/
/Print "Left corner?"/
//
/Limit Bob 320,0 To 640,200/


well... this is a Amos bug! :) There is (was) a stupid bug in the coordinates
check routine...

Limit Bob x,y To x1,y1

if the x coord is greater than the y1 coord, you'll get a 'illegal function
call'
:)) Now fixed.... remember that the x and x1 coords will be rounded up to the
nearest 16-pixels boundary.


Enjoy!


--


Bye!

Hi listers,

_Dozens_ of people have been sending me remarks and questions about IMPERATOR,
apparently one of the most popular games ever made in AMOS!

First thing I wish to say is: Thanks to all of you! Keep sending 'em in, as
such feedback is vital in the process of enhancing a product and briging it
closer to the user's wishes. You are the makers of Imperator 2!

Here are answers to the most Frequently Asked Questions on IMPERATOR:

/Q: Is Imperator commercial or shareware?/

A: Imperator is a commercial game. It will be published by Epic Marketing and
will come at least in English and German. Epic plan to release it at the
Cologne fair (13-15. November).
The demo you found on AmigaFlame states that the game is shareware, but this
is no longer true. Only the French version is still shareware and I have the
right to distribute it myself.

/Q: Was Imperator actually made using AMOS?/

A: Absolutely. It was entirely written in AMOSPro2, with a hint of Turbo and
Craft. (The gfx were made with PPaint)

/Q: Has the game been reviewed by magazines yet?/

A: Apart from France, where it got 2 enthusiastic reviews, not yet - to the
best of my knowledge. You can read the preview on AmigaFlame, or... send me
questions! Epic Marketing are in charge of the communication process and they
plan to have the game reviewed in every Amiga mag in the World.

/Q: Any differences between the shareware and commercial versions?/

A: The major difference is the music. It has been rewritten by Ruben Monteiro,
probably the greatest musician on the Amiga scene. (He volunteered to write
the music and you bet I accepted his offer :-) )
The dialogues (in English) have been rewritten by John Girvin.
There are a few other cosmetic differences.

/Q: Why are the Barbaric opponents so stupid?/

A: Because they are so superior in terms of brute force, they can't be made
too clever, otherwise the game would be downright unplayable. Anyway most of
your enemies in the full game are much tougher than the ones in the demo.

/Q: Is Imperator playable by modem?/

A: That could make sense for the tactical part (the battles) but it wouldn't
for the strategy. However, I'm considering the option of making a standalone
battle-module that would be playable by modem. _If_ that idea gets enough
support.

/Q: What about AGA gfx for Imperator?/

A: I have yet to find an AMOS extension that handles AGA completely and
without bugs... Any suggestions?


*Imperator (preview and demo) on AmigaFlame:*

http://www.amigaflame.co.uk/amii.htm

Please keep sending me remarks and suggestions!

Greets,

--
#Bernie Noel#, maker of *IMPERATOR*
Email: <bnoel@club-internet.fr>
--

	Message #1062 of 8185

AMOS page...

Sat Sep 12, 1998 5:23 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


Hello. I notice we have several new people on the list, so just thought
I'd give the URL for my AMOS page:
http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam/AMOS.HTM

It hasn't been updated since spring and there isn't much there, but if
you need a good development tool for grabbing bobs/sprites/icons,
then you'll definitely want to check out the AutoImageGrabber.
This utility will scan an .IFF picture and automatically grab the
images and store them in the appropriate bank. It's easy, fast and
effective... (72k .LHA file)

Anyway, I think there is also a very simple source for reading the
mouse directly through hardware and a bit of reading...

Actually, I have tons of old source, utilities, games, etc. and some
day I might put them on my page. :)


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

LDOS - Arexx

Wed Sep 16, 1998 8:55 am
"Declan Gorman" <declan_gorman@modusmedia.com>


Greetings,
I am trying to convert the following Arexx script to work with AMOS Pro
using the LDOS extension.

/*In OctaMED, switch Midi On*/
address octamed_rexx
op_set midiactive on

I have tested this script and it works fine when run from the CLI. My
conversion into AMOS Pro, using the LDOS extension, is as follows.

HOST$="OCTAMED_REXX"+Chr$(0)
MESSAGE$="op_set midiactive on"+Chr$(0)

FAIL=Arexx Exist(HOST$)
If FAIL=0
Print "Port cannot be found":End
End If

Print "OCTAMED_REXX is available."

MSG$=Lrexx Send Msg(HOST$,MESSAGE$,0)


AMOS does recognise the OctaMED arexx port but does not seem to send the
command. I have tried typing the command various different ways but nothing
seems to work. Can anyone help?

Declan.

p.s.
You have no idea what this would do to my current project if I got it
working......

	Message #1104 of 8185 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Audio-Digitizer

Wed Sep 16, 1998 7:18 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

>> In the techno Sound manual it explanes how to make a sampling prog.
I
>> tried doing one in amos, but its crap - if you try recording it to
>> doesn't record propperly at all (must be amos' slow Peek/Poke speed).
If
>> you put the output to lines you get a nice ocillascope effect though!
>>
>> I can post a copy if you want.

> Yes, post it !
> Is that proggy AMOS1.3 compatible ?


Ok, sorry about the delay, but here it is ;)

And yes, it does work with 1.3

--------------------------------------------------


Screen Open 0,320,256,2,Lowres
Double Buffer : Autoback 0


Poke $BFE301,0
Poke $BFD200,6
Poke $BFD000,2
'
' This sets the sampler up
'
'


Do

Plot 0,128

For A=0 To 320
P=Peek($BFE101)
'This reads the current volume
'

Draw To A,P
Next

Screen Swap
Wait Vbl
Cls 0

Loop

--------------------------------------------------


See ya.
--

Turbo Plus news.

Wed Sep 16, 1998 11:26 pm
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


Well, after a little learning and a few suggestions, I've decided on a few
things regarding Turbo Plus, it's distribution, and the doc's. ReAd oN:

1. Although my site (Parrottsoft) hasn't been finished yet, I have pretty
much decided on the final 'design', or layout if you will, for it.
Therefore, I've pretty much decided to put up the main section first, and
then the other areas will come after. This being the case, I'll make an
area in the -Downloads- section for Turbo Plus AND the docs. You can
download and distribute the disks (.DMS) -AND- the docs all you want!

2. To those who haven't gotten, didn't get, or still want Turbo Plus, I'll
still send it to you if you want, but it'll be MUCH easier for you to wait
a bit longer and go download everything off the site. I may even setup an
area for you to read the doc's on-line as well (another convenience).

BTW: Anyone that -does- download the disks and plans to distribute them
from their site, please tell me or Rune (Amos Factory) so we'll know. :)
..I think this should cover it. Just awhile more on those docs. :D

Change Mouse M

Thu Sep 17, 1998 3:10 am
Jeff Coney <coney@socs.murdoch.edu.au>


I can't get the instruction CHANGE MOUSE M to work properly.

Setting M to values from 1 to 3 invokes in turn the three mouse pointers
provided as standard. However, the manual states that setting M equal to
values larger than 3 also allows the pointer to assume the form of an image
from the sprite bank. The image is indexed by i=M-3. Thus, setting M=4
will result in the mouse pointer being taken from Image 1 in the sprite
bank, for example.

This does not work.

Can anyone help??

Jeff

On 16-Sep-98, Jeff Coney wrote:
>I can't get the instruction CHANGE MOUSE M to work properly.
>This does not work.
>Can anyone help??

"There are rules to every game." - Conan The Destroyer

_How to_
Bobs/sprites *must* be in 4 colour, low resolution. /16X16 is easiest/.

To mess with the colours, you use:

Colour 17 (light) default $EC8
Colour 18 (medium) default $EA0
Colour 19 (dark) default $C60

Re: Hard drive.

Thu Jan 1, 1970 7:59 am
(Keith Hill) <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


To the one known as Phil,
> > Urk, I invalidated my hard drive today, and have currently BARELY got
> > it back. The backup routines aren't working, and it is ridiculously
> > fragile.
> > This is a public service announcement:
> > Make a backup now !
> > Anyone got any good disk tools that work with AFS ?
> I'm sorry to say, that your root of your problm is probally due to , the
> nasty AFS system you use :/ I have heard of many a person on IRC sursing
> beacuse they have lost thier data, beacuse 'Of THE DAM AFS SYSTEM, CURCE

I invalidated my hard drive EVERY DAY with FFS, AFS, well, it's twice a
year, and you can almost always get yer files back quickly. Trouble is,
when it breaks, it breaks hard. Quarterback won't back it up at the mo.
In a few days (next time I see my friend with a few spare gig on the drive)
I'll be copying the whole partition over, reformat, and back again.

> YOU!', I don't know of any way to get your data back, the only thing i can
> suggest, is you grit and bear the problrm, and instakll FFS (fast File
> System) the amiga's defualt drriver, it is a lot, better, I have un
> validated my Hard drive Countless times (about 50 off the top of my head)
> and I have all ways got all the data back off my Hard drive, using disksalv,
> I also suggest that you install Disksafe (search aminet for 'disksafe') this
> program captures the harddrive's bitamp (or something) and helps stopping
> the drive getting invalidated, since i installed it , i have only hafd to
> use disksalv 1'nce , and that onyl 1 time, not the usal 3 , no fun with a
> 1.2 gig hd :/

Interesting. Not familiar with that proggie. I never got on well with ffs.
Slow, nasty. At the mo, I have some of my drives AFS, and some FFS. It works,
and I hardly ever (twice a year !) get problems with any of the drives, and
I have an almost complete backup on other partitions. Unfortunately, the backup
suddenly failed for no good reason this time (it says the archive is corrupt
when it validates it) so I'm stuck with the data in the mess it is. At least
I bypassed the problem. AFS has the lovely :.deldir, and the lovely
removedirentry program, which are lifesavers.

FFS really did invalidate like every day. I was spending two hours loading the
machine on a regular basis, and running disksalv (or qbtools) every week or so
for a day and a half. AFS really helps.

I'd say FFS is more software recoverable, and MUCH more prone to problems, but
AFS has fewer problems, and the data is practically ALWAYS copy-recoverable.
I want a disksalv proggie for AFS.

Re: Change Mouse M

Thu Sep 17, 1998 8:46 pm
<Minion2197@aol.com>


In order for the instruction CHANGE MOUSE to work , you sprite/bob must be
defined as 4 colour (2 plane) bob. I had this problem for years. Id only use 2
or 3 coluors in my bobs, but they were defined as 16 colour(4 plane) bobs.
Check your bobs, that`ll be your problem !
