	Message #1121 of 8185

Re: Which Monitor?

Fri Sep 18, 1998 11:41 am
"Ives, Neil, IVESNJ" <neil.ives@bt.com>


> From: "Declan Gorman" <declan_gorman@modusmedia.com>

> I am considering buying a monitor for my Amiga and am wondering which
would
> be the best one to buy.

> I would like one that displays standard and large screens with ease,
priced
> around £300 sterling.

> Any help would be appreciated.

> Declan.

I have had a Microvitec Multisync monitor with my 1200 for about 3 years. It
dynamically autoswitches resolution. The cost is somewhere in the region
you mention. I am at work writing this but If you like I will have a look in
Amiga Format for a supplier & a price.
I originally used Commodores Euro72 or Multiscan Productivity modes with
this monitor, but I was a little disappointed to discover that the display
left a grey strip on either side. My monitor has vertical but no horizontal
adjustment so I was unable to do anything about it.. To minimise the effect
I used 'Neagrey' in the startup sequence, this just clears the unused
display to black, which looked a lot better. However, I recently found a new
version of Super72 display driver, (mail me for a copy) which I use in
hi-res laced 800x600 with excellent results. The screen is now fully filled.

I have seen adverts for scan doublers which claim to allow you to use
cheaper PC monitors. I don't know all the pros & cons of these, perhaps
someone else on the list can comment.
Regards.
Neil Ives.

	Message #1124 of 8185

Turbo Plus Questions.

Sat Sep 19, 1998 3:38 am
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


Someone asked me (sorry, I forget who atm) what Turbo Plus IS and what type
of commands it offers. I thought I would breifly answer: Turbo Plus,
successor to the Craft Extension, is basically a set of 'turbo' commands:

Graphical (which makes up the bulk of it)..
3D Drawing, Zones, Starfields, Vector Objects,
Blocks, Icons, Scrolling, Scenes, and Bitplane;

Also many Miscellaneous and Bitwise Operations.
Comes complete with Scene Editor and IFF Font maker.

It features commands such as:

F Plot, =F Point, F Draw, F Draw To, F Circle, R Home, R Bar, Blit Clear;
Set Planes, Plane Offset, Plane Swap, Plane Shift Up/Down, Plane Update;
Reserve Stars, Define Star, Display Stars, Stars Draw, Stars Speed/Erase;
Scene Load, Scene Convert, Scene Copy, Scene Fill, Scene Bank, etc.;
Bilt Int On, Blit Int Off, Blit Int Wait, Blit Int Change and MANY more.

As I have reported, I am working on getting the docs scanned and saved off
into .jpg format. I've also been talking with Rune (webmaster of the Amos
Factory) into getting the coverdisk copies I sent out onto the site. When
either of these happen, the List will be informed. If anyone has any
FURTHER questions regarding Turbo PLus, please mail me. If you have any
questions regarding commands, etc., please wait till the docs are up.

Adam Parrott, mailto: parrotta@usa.net, ICQ# 12967025, Handle: Axianator
Webmaster of Parrottsoft and proud member of Team *AMOS* and the IAPA.
The official Parrottsoft site at http://parrottsoft.hypermart.net up soon!

	Message #1128 of 8185 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: LDOS - Arexx

Sat Sep 19, 1998 8:54 am
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 16-Sep-98, Declan Gorman wrote:

DG> I am trying to convert the following Arexx script to work with AMOS
Pro
DG> using the LDOS extension.

DG> /*In OctaMED, switch Midi On*/
DG> address octamed_rexx
DG> op_set midiactive on

DG> I have tested this script and it works fine when run from the CLI. My
DG> conversion into AMOS Pro, using the LDOS extension, is as follows.

DG> HOST$="OCTAMED_REXX"+Chr$(0)

Arexx host names are _case sensitive_, maybe there is a bug in Arexx Exist
command which tells you that port exists, but when you want to send
command, it won't work... Also, are you sure that you need Chr$(0) ?

DG> MESSAGE$="op_set midiactive on"+Chr$(0)

DG> FAIL=Arexx Exist(HOST$)
DG> If FAIL=0
DG> Print "Port cannot be found":End
DG> End If

DG> Print "OCTAMED_REXX is available."

DG> MSG$=Lrexx Send Msg(HOST$,MESSAGE$,0)

DG> AMOS does recognise the OctaMED arexx port but does not seem to send
the
DG> command. I have tried typing the command various different ways but
nothing
DG> seems to work. Can anyone help?

Try typing in CLI

tco
ts

and see what is realy sent, and where. You can also try monitoring with
SnoopDos3.0 .

If everything else fails you can always use

Exec "RX "+chr$(34)+"address octamed_rexx ; op_set midiactive on"+chr$(34)

Regards

Re: Hard drive.

Sat Sep 19, 1998 9:03 am
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 18-Sep-98, Andrew Crowe wrote:

AC> I think the easiest way to avoid devalidation is to find which programs
AC> are crashing it and replace them for ones that work propperly;)

There is a program called DiskSafe (disk/salv/DiskSafe.lha) which captures
reset signal, caused by both keyboard or software, and delays reset long
enough to write bitmaps. I think that is *the* solution, however it
doesn't work on every Amiga...

AC> And a program like MultiReset helps too, it writes the bitmap *and* can
AC> show a little pic and play a sound when you reset :)

I don't like such programs. I want do do something on the computer while it
validates ;)

Regards

	Message #1133 of 8185

Re: Load images

Sun Sep 20, 1998 2:17 am
Andy H <geosync@ozemail.com.au>


Hi Nikola,

The only problem with using animation is they take up huge chunks of
memory. Keep going with the Load iff idea. I used it in StarFighter
for all my cut scenes. To get the best frame rate you need to use
'addbuffers' using the Exec command to the drive you are loading
multiple images from. Also letter-box the image down to about 320*192,
this gives a bit more speed. You can load up to HAM 5 images though the
best rates are achieved using 64 colours or lower.
Andy H.
> f> I would like to know how to do to load images, as fast as possible.
> f> No matter the time it will take to create and save the pix, I want
> f> the fastest load. No matter either the size of the file(s), the
> f> images will be loaded from hard disk or DCrom.
> f> I'm trying to simulate video sequences in a game, the only way I know
> f> is "Load Iff" in a loop, but it is sllloooooowwwww (about 3 frames/sec)

John Bintz <uv334@victoria.tc.ca>


Or, you can develop an animation stream player, which loads one frame from
the animation at a time. Use the Frame Load command with a section of
memory, then double-buffer pate the new shot on the screen. I have a 3.5
meg anim I made for the (non-existant) CD-ROM version of Final
Existence, which plays at about 12 FPS (from an original 15) direct from a
SCSI Zip disk. Play around with that, and i fyou need code, I'll putll it
out and post it up.

Re: Audio-Digitizer

Sun Sep 20, 1998 3:00 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

>> In the techno Sound manual it explanes how to make a sampling prog.
I
>> tried doing one in amos, but its crap - if you try recording it to
>> doesn't record propperly at all (must be amos' slow Peek/Poke speed).
If
>> you put the output to lines you get a nice ocillascope effect though!
>>
>> I can post a copy if you want.

> Yes, post it !
> Is that proggy AMOS1.3 compatible ?


Ok, sorry about the delay, but here it is ;)

And yes, it does work with 1.3

--------------------------------------------------


Screen Open 0,320,256,2,Lowres
Double Buffer : Autoback 0


Poke $BFE301,0
Poke $BFD200,6
Poke $BFD000,2
'
' This sets the sampler up
'
'


Do

Plot 0,128

For A=0 To 320
P=Peek($BFE101)
'This reads the current volume
'

Draw To A,P
Next

Screen Swap
Wait Vbl
Cls 0

Loop

--------------------------------------------------


See ya.

Good/Bad/Ugly

Sun Sep 20, 1998 3:53 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


So, I was working on the SoloTrek III module editor and got busy on IRC. I
thought I'd shut AMOS down, so I fired it up and loaded the program. I didn't
mess with much code and saved it, then quit AMOS. A bit later, I couldn't
remember if AMOS was still running or not, so I flipped to it. It was, so I
closed it. I forgot that and tried to flip to it again. Lo and behold, another
AMOS was running!

No one mentioned this particular fix. Now you can run multiple copies of AMOS.
Beware!

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark

Date: 28 August 1998 09:09
Subject: [amos-list] Amos + Free Memory


>From: "Declan Gorman" <declan_gorman@modusmedia.com>
>
>Is there any way in AmosPro to tell how much free memory a user has.
>A program I am working on uses a user definable buffer. If the user
changes
>the buffer size, I want to check the new buffer size against the amount of
>free memory and either allow or disallow the change dependant on the amount
>of free memory.
>
>Thanks in advance.
>
>Declan.
>
>
>
Yes, the amount of free memory can be found by adding CHIP FREE to FAST
FREE, e.g:

MEM=Chip Free + Fast Free

Read the bloody manual!

Re: Hey! Ne1 Like Joysticks?

Tue Sep 15, 1998 8:29 am
"Infinity Productions" <infinity_productions@lineone.net>


Hey, are you aware that the following SHORT section of code does EXACTLY the
same thing, only faster and with less stupid excess code?

J=Joy(1)
X=Sgn(J and 8)-Sgn(J and 4)
Y=Sgn(J and 2)-Sgn(J and 1)

-----Original Message-----
From: John Glanville <John.Glanville@btinternet.com>
To: amos-list@onelist.com <amos-list@onelist.com>
Date: 01 September 1998 23:36
Subject: [amos-list] Hey! Ne1 Like Joysticks?


Hey! Look! At this… Ne1 want a piece of code that turns the joystick input 2
+ or -..

Eg.

J=Joy(1) ;J=2 ; Joystick is Down!

K=J-2 ;k=0

P#=J/4.0 ;P#=0.5

P=P# ;P=0

I=Sgn(J) ;I=1

if P#=P ;This isn’t true 0.5<>0

X=Sgn(J-6)*I

End If

If P=0 ;This is true

Y=I*(K+K+1) ;Y=1

End If

Say you push the joystick up it returns y=-1 X=0!

If You Push Joystick Left then X=-1 Y=0

If You Push Joystick left Diagonally Up X=-1 and Y=-1

You Could use this in a game!! Something similar 2 tron!

Where U only need the direction in +1’s or –1’s!

I’ve used it and found it gets rid of annoying and slow If statements!!!!

Or U could just Delete this as it is a pointless waste of Virtual Paper!
Unless You have printed it in which case! Help!

"Declan Gorman" <declan_gorman@modusmedia.com>


The Arexx command TCO or TS do not display any entries for Arexx commands

What does this suggest?

Exec "RX "+chr$(34)+"address octamed_rexx op_set midiactive on"+chr$(34)

anyway.

Declan.

-----Original Message-----
From: Nikola Smolenski [mailto:smolensk@EUnet.yu]
Sent: 19 September 1998 08:55
To: amos-list@onelist.com
Subject: [amos-list] Re: LDOS - Arexx


From: Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>

On 16-Sep-98, Declan Gorman wrote:

DG> I am trying to convert the following Arexx script to work with AMOS
Pro
DG> using the LDOS extension.

DG> /*In OctaMED, switch Midi On*/
DG> address octamed_rexx
DG> op_set midiactive on

DG> I have tested this script and it works fine when run from the CLI. My
DG> conversion into AMOS Pro, using the LDOS extension, is as follows.

DG> HOST$="OCTAMED_REXX"+Chr$(0)

Arexx host names are _case sensitive_, maybe there is a bug in Arexx Exist
command which tells you that port exists, but when you want to send
command, it won't work... Also, are you sure that you need Chr$(0) ?

DG> MESSAGE$="op_set midiactive on"+Chr$(0)

DG> FAIL=Arexx Exist(HOST$)
DG> If FAIL=0
DG> Print "Port cannot be found":End
DG> End If

DG> Print "OCTAMED_REXX is available."

DG> MSG$=Lrexx Send Msg(HOST$,MESSAGE$,0)

DG> AMOS does recognise the OctaMED arexx port but does not seem to send
the
DG> command. I have tried typing the command various different ways but
nothing
DG> seems to work. Can anyone help?

Try typing in CLI

tco
ts

and see what is realy sent, and where. You can also try monitoring with
SnoopDos3.0 .

If everything else fails you can always use

Exec "RX "+chr$(34)+"address octamed_rexx ; op_set midiactive on"+chr$(34)

Regards
--

Re: Whatta heck?

Tue Sep 22, 1998 9:37 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

On 22-Sep-98, Sasu Lintula wrote something which is obviously worth
replying to:
> From: Sasu Lintula <samali@utu.fi>

> After installing turbo-ext my Amy has been very unstable. Every time I
leave Amos or only switch to Workbench Guru starts to meditate. What's
wrong with turbo?

> Another thing is that the Compiler doesn't want to compile those
turbo-commands. Have I done something wrong?

Are you using F Paste Icon? These work rather badly, although fast.
There seems to be a bug in it which causes it to write to the wrong part
of mem or something.

You should use F 16proc Icon / F 32proc Icon as these have no such
problems.

(I think its a bug in the blitter routines or something)


And with the compiler, is there an S drawer in your amospro drawer?
If there is then go to interpriter config, load default config and save
it in S:

Then delete the S drawer in AMOSPro drawer, that should fix it I think.

See ya.

Re: LDOS - Arexx

Thu Sep 24, 1998 8:32 am
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 22-Sep-98, Declan Gorman wrote:

DG> The Arexx command TCO or TS do not display any entries for Arexx
commands
DG> sent from AMOSPro using LDOS. It does display info on scripts I
execute
DG> from the CLI.

DG> What does this suggest?

If LDOS should send commands in a standard way (which means that it would
not work without RexxMast), that means that commands aren't sent. If it
sends commands to Arexx port directly (like e.g. scmsg), that still
doesn't means anything.

Are you sure that you don't need to somehow 'Open' port before sending
messages to it? If you are, then... I don't have LDOS, and I realy don't
know what is the problem, sorry.

DG> Exec "RX "+chr$(34)+"address octamed_rexx op_set midiactive
on"+chr$(34)
DG> works fine but slows down my program, so is not a realistic option.

/Maybe/ it would help if you make RX resident.

	Message #1170 of 8185

Re: SV: [amos-list] Re: Amos - the PC version

Thu Sep 24, 1998 7:38 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


>> the version I intended to write was an AMOS on the PC that you could
>> directly port all origanal AMOS progs over to and use... code, banks,
>> sprites, mods, etc. with little or no conversion required.
> Yea! I have waited for the PC version of AMOS since I got my first
> PC! Dont wait, just DO IT!

Yeah, don't wait... just DO IT!!
How far along are you? What PC language will you be using (C,
C++, Assembler, etc)?? Will you be creating an interpreter,
RunTime Environment, true compiler, etc???

I had actually planned on making an AMOS to BLITZ source
convertor at some point, but Paul Burkey has already started on
such a program (which I think the first version may already be on
Aminet)... and now after listening to my brother and many other
people complain about the lack of a PC AMOS style language
(combined with the fact that I now do almost all of my programming
on my PC), I am considering working on an AMOS compatible PC
language... not 100% compatible as I wouldn't include that horrible
Amal subset language and probably would force the use of a
Bob Clear... Bob Draw structure.


Anyway, I think that by using C and Allegro, a programmer could
easily create an AMOS style language, but obviously you would
need many support utilities: graphic convertors, data bank
convertors, sound convertors, music convertors, etc.

The point is there would be a lot of work involved in such a project,
which is probably why no one has finished an AMOS compatible PC
language yet... they start and make reasonably good progress, but I
think they haven't planned out the project, so when they keep finding
more and more sub-projects that need to be completed, they
ultimately end up "burnt out" and say "the heck with it!".
Bear in mind, this is just my opinion, but I imagine that's pretty
close to what actually happens.

Anyway, I would be interested in hearing your plans for this PC
equivalent of AMOS... perhaps this is something we could work
on as a group project. Define the whole project, EXACTLY WHAT
NEEDS TO BE DONE, list these items (parsing, conversion utilities,
code generation, support libraries for audio-video, etc.) and then
let four or five PC programmers each take one task and work on
it. Once completed, we grab another task until soon we have it all
done and behind us... instead of continually hearing people ask
"Where can I find a PC AMOS?" and saying "there is none, but
maybe we could make one", we could finally say "Here, try this!!"

What do you think?


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

	Message #1189 of 8185

Bob Off alternative

Mon Sep 28, 1998 5:35 pm
"Service" <service@emed.com>


I think there might've been a question in the past about
turning off specified BOBs related to the Bob Draw command.
Here's a technique if anyone's interested:

Here's the simplest way of drawing a Bob on screen:
Bob n,x,y,image
Bob Draw

Since there is no such command as Bob Off n,
how about re-locating the Bob out of view.
Example: on a 320x200 screen
Bob n, 350,0,image

This is assuming you don't have a super-wide Bob,
if that's the case just increase x-postition.
Of, course it depends on the Hot Spot how far the Bob is positioned
off screen so that no part of the image is appearing on screen.
If the Hot Spot of the Bob is at 0,0 you could
Bob n,321,0,image.

But you guys and gals probably already knew this,

Laterz,
Ken

	Message #1190 of 8185

Dim array() problem.

Mon Sep 28, 1998 11:03 pm
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


While in AMOS lately I quickly compiled a program I was working on and ran
it. Much to my surprise, it didn't get past the first few instructions (it
returned an "Illegal function call"). I went back, did some debugging and
found it was a Dim statement I had made to an array. Here's an excerpt:

Set Buffer 1024..
Dim _VAR(G*5,G*5) (G=64)

I made a small program to see if I could solve the problem and found that
nothing over G*3 worked, even if the Buffer was over 5000k! Assuming my
calculator doesn't lie: 64*5=320, 320^2=102400, 102400/1024=100k, which
tells me that a Set Buffer 1024 should be more than enough. :/

I was just wondering if anyone could help with this problem. I have one or
two ideas, but since I'm not at my Amiga, I have yet to try them. If anyone
has a quick solution or sees something I've missed, please mail. Thanks.

Adam Parrott, mailto: parrotta@usa.net, ICQ# 12967025, Handle: Axianator
Webmaster of Parrottsoft and proud member of Team *AMOS* and the IAPA.
The official Parrottsoft site at http://parrottsoft.hypermart.net up soon!

Re: Dim array() problem.

Tue Sep 29, 1998 12:12 am
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

On 28-Sep-98, Adam Parrott wrote something which is obviously worth
replying to:
> From: "Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>

> While in AMOS lately I quickly compiled a program I was working on and
ran
> it. Much to my surprise, it didn't get past the first few instructions
(it
> returned an "Illegal function call"). I went back, did some debugging
and
> found it was a Dim statement I had made to an array. Here's an
excerpt:

> Set Buffer 1024..
> Dim _VAR(G*5,G*5) (G=64)

Ah yes, I had this problem too. It seems that AMOS doesn't like dim'ing
anything with over a certain ammount of arays. The only way to get
around this is using a memory bank insted.

eg. Reserve as work 5,(G*5)*(G*5)+10

This'll save memory and speed.

>returned an "Illegal function call"). I went back, did some debugging and
>found it was a Dim statement I had made to an array. Here's an excerpt:
>Set Buffer 1024..
>Dim _VAR(G*5,G*5) (G=64)

Hmmm, I'm pretty sure I've made arrays waaaay bigger than that (although it
had many more levels/subscripts/arguments/whatever they're called). I'll
have to check when I get home.

Phil 8-)

>around this is using a memory bank insted.
